We\\\\u2019ll keep things practical, with registrar-specific examples, copy\\\\u2011paste command checks, and a troubleshooting matrix.\\\\n\\\\nAccording to the official feature set, you can deploy a Manus web app quickly and connect a custom domain as part of the publishing workflow, with built\\\\u2011in analytics and version control for safe iterations, as described on the Manus Web Apps features page and release announcement for Manus 1.5. See the claims on the platform\\\\u2019s own pages: [Manus Web Apps features (2025)](https://manus.im/features/webapp) and [Introducing Manus 1.5 (2025)](https://manus.im/blog/manus-1.5-release).\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Who this guide is for\\\\n\\\\n* No\\\\u2011code founders and marketers who want a clear, clickable path without deep DNS knowledge\\\\n* Indie developers who appreciate exact record types, TTL guidance, and command-line validations\\\\n* SMB teams shipping quickly on a branded domain and caring about rollback and reliability\\\\n\\\\nYou\\\\u2019ll learn to:\\\\n\\\\n* Decide between subdomain (recommended first) and apex domain\\\\n* Add the right DNS records (CNAME vs A/ALIAS/ANAME)\\\\n* Validate propagation and SSL with dig, nslookup, and curl\\\\n* Set up canonical redirects (www \\\\u2194 apex) without loops\\\\n* Plan a safe cutover and rollback using versions\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Prerequisites\\\\n\\\\n* A Manus 1.5 app ready to publish\\\\n* Access to your domain registrar or DNS provider (Cloudflare, Namecheap, Route 53, etc.)\\\\n* Permissions in Manus to publish and configure domains within your workspace\\\\n* The willingness to copy the exact domain target shown in the Manus UI (don\\\\u2019t guess values)\\\\n\\\\nNote: Specific UI labels in Manus (e.g., \\\\u201cPublish\\\\u201d \\\\u2192 \\\\u201cDomain\\\\u201d) can change. When in doubt, follow the on\\\\u2011screen hints and copy the domain target exactly as shown.\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Quick DNS glossary (you\\\\u2019ll use these terms)\\\\n\\\\n* A record: Points a hostname to an IPv4 address. Example: example.com \\\\u2192 203.0.113.10\\\\n* CNAME: Points a hostname to another hostname. Example: app.example.com \\\\u2192 host.platform.com\\\\n* ALIAS/ANAME: Provider-specific record types that behave like a CNAME at the apex (root) domain.\\\\n* Apex domain (root): example.com (no prefix). Standards don\\\\u2019t allow a CNAME here; use A/ALIAS/ANAME or redirect to a subdomain.\\\\n\\\\nIf you want a quick fundamentals refresher for DNS and custom domains, skim our concise overview of [DNS basics (A vs CNAME, MX, TXT) and custom domain setup](https://skywork.ai/skypage/en/Universe-Website-Builder%3A-An-SEO-Expert%27s-AI-Deep-Dive/1976116349397692416).\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Decision: Start with a subdomain or go straight to apex?\\\\n\\\\n* Subdomain first (recommended): app.example.com or www.example.com\\\\n  + Easiest path: create a CNAME pointing to the Manus\\\\u2011provided hostname\\\\n  + Flexible: platform can change infrastructure without you chasing IPs\\\\n* Apex domain (example.com): more moving parts\\\\n  + You can\\\\u2019t use a standard CNAME at apex\\\\n  + You\\\\u2019ll need ALIAS/ANAME (if supported), Cloudflare CNAME Flattening, or A records (only if Manus provides static IPs)\\\\n  + If none fit, redirect apex \\\\u2192 www and point www (CNAME) to Manus\\\\n\\\\nCloudflare documents CNAME flattening for apex use, and explains apex limitations and TTL behavior in its developer docs. See the relevant guides: [Cloudflare CNAME Flattening](https://developers.cloudflare.com/dns/cname-flattening/set-up-cname-flattening/) and the [Cloudflare DNS records how\\\\u2011to](https://developers.cloudflare.com/dns/manage-dns-records/how-to/create-dns-records/).\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Step-by-step: Map a subdomain to Manus (recommended first deployment)\\\\n\\\\nThe subdomain path is straightforward and resilient. We\\\\u2019ll show the flow, then give Cloudflare and Namecheap examples.\\\\n\\\\n1. Find your domain target in Manus\\\\n\\\\n* Open your Manus 1.5 app.\\\\n* Navigate to the area where you publish or manage the app\\\\u2019s domain. Copy the CNAME target value Manus displays for your custom domain. The label may read \\\\u201cDomain,\\\\u201d \\\\u201cPublish,\\\\u201d or similar.\\\\n\\\\n2. Choose a subdomain\\\\n\\\\n* Common picks: app.example.com, www.example.com, or beta.example.com\\\\n\\\\n3. Create a CNAME record at your DNS provider\\\\n\\\\n* Name/Host: the subdomain part (e.g., app or www)\\\\n* Type: CNAME\\\\n* Target: paste the exact Manus hostname you copied\\\\n* TTL: Auto or 300 seconds during setup\\\\n\\\\n4. Wait for propagation and verify (details later in this guide)\\\\n5. Confirm SSL/HTTPS shows as active in Manus after validation completes\\\\n\\\\nWhy CNAME? Because Manus can update its underlying IPs transparently; your record continues to resolve to the right place without manual IP updates. For a primer on record types, see [DNSimple\\\\u2019s record differences explainer](https://support.dnsimple.com/articles/differences-between-a-cname-alias-url/) (2025).\\\\n\\\\n### Example: Cloudflare\\\\n\\\\n* Cloudflare dashboard \\\\u2192 DNS \\\\u2192 Records \\\\u2192 Add record \\\\u2192 Type: CNAME\\\\n* Name: app (or www)\\\\n* Target: the Manus hostname from the Manus UI\\\\n* TTL: Auto\\\\n* Save\\\\n\\\\nCloudflare\\\\u2019s step-by-step DNS record creation flow is documented here: [Cloudflare: Create DNS records](https://developers.cloudflare.com/dns/manage-dns-records/how-to/create-dns-records/).\\\\n\\\\n### Example: Namecheap\\\\n\\\\n* Namecheap Dashboard \\\\u2192 Domain List \\\\u2192 your domain \\\\u2192 Manage \\\\u2192 Advanced DNS \\\\u2192 Host Records \\\\u2192 Add New Record\\\\n* Type: CNAME Record\\\\n* Host: app (or www)\\\\n* Value: Manus hostname from the Manus UI\\\\n* TTL: Automatic \\\\u2192 Save\\\\n\\\\nNamecheap\\\\u2019s knowledge base describes CNAME host records and URL redirects. Refer to Namecheap: set up host records and, for redirects, Namecheap: URL redirect.\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Option: Put the apex domain (example.com) on Manus\\\\n\\\\nBecause you can\\\\u2019t use a normal CNAME at the apex, choose one of these:\\\\n\\\\n* ALIAS/ANAME at apex: If your DNS provider supports it, point @ to the Manus hostname\\\\n* Cloudflare CNAME Flattening: Set @ to the Manus hostname and enable flattening so resolvers see A/AAAA\\\\n* A/AAAA records: Only if Manus publicly provides static IPs (not common for multi\\\\u2011tenant platforms)\\\\n* Redirect apex \\\\u2192 www: Keep an easy CNAME on www \\\\u2192 Manus, and forward example.com to https://www.example.com\\\\n\\\\nCloudflare explains flattening and apex handling in its docs: [CNAME Flattening](https://developers.cloudflare.com/dns/cname-flattening/set-up-cname-flattening/) and [Create zone apex record](https://developers.cloudflare.com/dns/manage-dns-records/how-to/create-zone-apex/).\\\\n\\\\nIf none of these apply to your provider or Manus target type, use the redirect approach. Cloudflare supports both Page Rules and Bulk Redirects with path preservation, as described in [Bulk Redirects (www redirect how\\\\u2011to)](https://developers.cloudflare.com/pages/how-to/www-redirect/) and [URL forwarding with Page Rules](https://developers.cloudflare.com/rules/page-rules/how-to/url-forwarding/).\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## SSL/HTTPS: what to expect\\\\n\\\\nModern platforms typically issue SSL certificates automatically via an ACME provider after your DNS validates. Timelines are usually minutes\\\\u2014not hours\\\\u2014once DNS is correct. For context on ACME issuance and challenge types, see the Let\\\\u2019s Encrypt resources on [challenge types](https://letsencrypt.org/docs/challenge-types/) and a typical issuance flow (around a couple of minutes) as illustrated in the [Linode acme.sh guide](https://www.linode.com/docs/guides/secure-website-lets-encrypt-acme-sh/) (examples circa 2024\\\\u20132025).\\\\n\\\\nPractical advice:\\\\n\\\\n* Expect SSL to change from \\\\u201cPending\\\\u201d to \\\\u201cActive\\\\u201d within minutes after DNS resolves\\\\n* If it stalls, re\\\\u2011check your CNAME and whether the validation endpoint is reachable\\\\n* After HTTPS is active, test for mixed content issues (hardcoded http:// assets)\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Verify DNS and SSL like a pro\\\\n\\\\nUse multiple resolvers (Cloudflare 1.1.1.1, Google 8.8.8.8) and quick HTTP checks.\\\\n\\\\nDNS checks:\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\ndig @1.1.1.1 app.example.com CNAME\\\\ndig @8.8.8.8 example.com A\\\\nnslookup -type=CNAME app.example.com\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\nHTTP/redirect checks:\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\ncurl -I https://app.example.com\\\\ncurl -I http://www.example.com  # expect 301 \\\\u2192 https://example.com if redirect in place\\\\n\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\nPropagation realities: Many changes are visible within minutes, but global caches can take longer. Cloudflare documents TTL behavior (proxied records often present quickly, but other caches must expire) in its [TTL reference](https://developers.cloudflare.com/dns/manage-dns-records/reference/ttl/). Traditional guidance for full internet propagation ranges from 24\\\\u201348 hours depending on TTL and resolver caches; see an overview in [SiteGround\\\\u2019s DNS propagation explainer](https://www.siteground.com/kb/dns-propagation/).\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Redirects and canonicalization (www \\\\u2194 apex)\\\\n\\\\nPick one canonical hostname and make everything else redirect there with 301s. Two common patterns:\\\\n\\\\n* Canonical is example.com\\\\n  + www.example.com \\\\u2192 https://example.com/$1\\\\n* Canonical is www.example.com\\\\n  + example.com \\\\u2192 https://www.example.com/$1\\\\n\\\\nCloudflare options:\\\\n\\\\n* Bulk Redirects: great for domain\\\\u2011wide rules with path preservation; see [Bulk Redirects](https://developers.cloudflare.com/pages/how-to/www-redirect/)\\\\n* Page Rules: quick URL forwarding; see [URL forwarding with Page Rules](https://developers.cloudflare.com/rules/page-rules/how-to/url-forwarding/)\\\\n\\\\nNamecheap option:\\\\n\\\\n* URL Redirect (per their KB) to forward apex \\\\u2194 www with 301 and path preservation; see Namecheap URL redirect\\\\n\\\\nAvoid loops by ensuring only one rule path exists for each direction and that both hostnames aren\\\\u2019t simultaneously pointed to different origins.\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Staging \\\\u2192 production and safe rollbacks\\\\n\\\\nA simple, low\\\\u2011risk approach:\\\\n\\\\n1. Stage on a subdomain\\\\n\\\\n* staging.example.com \\\\u2192 CNAME \\\\u2192 Manus hostname\\\\n* Low TTL (e.g., 300 seconds) to speed cutovers during launch\\\\n\\\\n2. Promote to production\\\\n\\\\n* Flip www.example.com (or app.example.com) to point to the stable build\\\\n* Keep a single canonical redirect policy to avoid loops\\\\n\\\\n3. Use Manus versions to revert fast\\\\n\\\\n* Manus 1.5 highlights tracked changes and the ability to revert to prior versions; this is ideal for rapid rollback if an update misbehaves, per the platform\\\\u2019s own materials in [Introducing Manus 1.5 (2025)](https://manus.im/blog/manus-1.5-release).\\\\n\\\\nFor additional process rigor around releases and rollbacks, read our primer on [versioning and rollback best practices](https://skywork.ai/blog/optimizing-developer-workflows-kat-dev-best-practices/).\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Planning and checklists (optional, but recommended)\\\\n\\\\nFor recurring launches, keep a lightweight, reusable checklist that covers DNS updates, redirect rules, SSL verification, analytics toggles, and permission checks. If you prefer to draft and refine checklists with an AI assistant, consider using [Skywork AI](https://skywork.ai/) to generate and iterate a go\\\\u2011live list.\\\\n\\\\nDisclosure: Skywork AI is our product.\\\\n\\\\nIf you\\\\u2019re building a more formal governance workflow (roles, approvals, data boundaries), a quick read on a pragmatic [security checklist before go\\\\u2011live](https://skywork.ai/blog/how-to-secure-your-agent-data/) can help you spot issues early.\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Troubleshooting matrix\\\\n\\\\nBelow are common symptoms, likely causes, and concrete fixes.\\\\n\\\\n1. My domain isn\\\\u2019t verifying or the app won\\\\u2019t load\\\\n\\\\n* Check for conflicting records: if you\\\\u2019re using a CNAME for www, remove any A record that also targets www\\\\n* Lower TTL ahead of changes to accelerate cache turnover; Cloudflare\\\\u2019s [TTL reference](https://developers.cloudflare.com/dns/manage-dns-records/reference/ttl/) explains how TTL affects visibility\\\\n* Validate on multiple resolvers:\\\\n\\\\n  ```\\\\n  dig @1.1.1.1 www.example.com CNAME\\\\n  dig @8.8.8.8 www.example.com CNAME\\\\n\\\\n  ```\\\\n* Ensure you copied the exact Manus hostname from the Manus UI (no typos, no trailing dot if your provider adds one automatically)\\\\n\\\\n2. SSL stuck on \\\\u201cPending\\\\u201d or browser shows insecure\\\\n\\\\n* Give it 10\\\\u201330 minutes after DNS resolves\\\\n* Confirm the CNAME resolves globally; re\\\\u2011issue if the UI allows\\\\n* Make sure any CDN/proxy is not blocking validation requests\\\\n* Typical ACME timelines are short; for context on challenges, see [Let\\\\u2019s Encrypt challenge types](https://letsencrypt.org/docs/challenge-types/)\\\\n\\\\n3. I\\\\u2019m seeing 525 or 526 errors behind Cloudflare\\\\n\\\\n* 525 (SSL handshake failed) often means the proxy can\\\\u2019t complete TLS with the origin; review your SSL mode and origin cert\\\\n  + Cloudflare explains causes/remedies in [Error 525](https://developers.cloudflare.com/support/troubleshooting/http-status-codes/cloudflare-5xx-errors/error-525/)\\\\n* 526 (Invalid SSL certificate) indicates the proxy can\\\\u2019t validate the origin certificate\\\\n  + See Cloudflare\\\\u2019s guidance in [Error 526](https://developers.cloudflare.com/support/troubleshooting/http-status-codes/cloudflare-5xx-errors/error-526/)\\\\n\\\\n4. Redirects don\\\\u2019t behave or I\\\\u2019m in a loop\\\\n\\\\n* Confirm a single canonical endpoint (either apex or www)\\\\n* Avoid stacking a Page Rule and a Bulk Redirect that duplicate logic in opposite directions\\\\n* Ensure both hostnames aren\\\\u2019t pointing to different origins simultaneously\\\\n\\\\n5. Mixed content warnings after enabling HTTPS\\\\n\\\\n* Update hardcoded http:// asset URLs to https://\\\\n* Use browser DevTools \\\\u2192 Security panel to identify non\\\\u2011secure requests\\\\n\\\\n6. I want the apex live, but my provider doesn\\\\u2019t support ALIAS/ANAME\\\\n\\\\n* Use Cloudflare\\\\u2019s CNAME Flattening if you\\\\u2019re comfortable moving DNS there; see [CNAME Flattening](https://developers.cloudflare.com/dns/cname-flattening/set-up-cname-flattening/)\\\\n* Otherwise, redirect apex \\\\u2192 www and keep www \\\\u2192 Manus via CNAME\\\\n\\\\n7. Propagation is taking forever\\\\n\\\\n* Some resolvers cache longer than expected; general web guidance pegs global propagation at 24\\\\u201348 hours depending on TTL and prior caches, as summarized by [SiteGround\\\\u2019s overview](https://www.siteground.com/kb/dns-propagation/)\\\\n* While waiting, query public resolvers directly and ask teammates in different regions to test\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Post\\\\u2011launch checks (5\\\\u2011minute sanity sweep)\\\\n\\\\n* DNS resolution: dig/nslookup show the expected answers on 1.1.1.1 and 8.8.8.8\\\\n* HTTP status: curl -I returns 200 on the canonical hostname, 301 on the non\\\\u2011canonical one\\\\n* SSL: padlock appears; no mixed content in DevTools\\\\n* Analytics: confirm the built\\\\u2011in analytics panel populates after initial traffic, a Manus 1.5 feature noted in the [release announcement](https://manus.im/blog/manus-1.5-release)\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## FAQs\\\\n\\\\nQ: Does Manus 1.5 natively support custom domains and fast deploys?\\\\n\\\\n* Yes. The platform advertises instant deploys and custom domain connection as part of web app publishing, along with analytics and version tracking. See [Manus Web Apps features](https://manus.im/features/webapp).\\\\n\\\\nQ: Should I start with www or app as my hostname?\\\\n\\\\n* Start with a subdomain you\\\\u2019re comfortable making canonical. www is common if you plan to move your root (apex) there eventually.\\\\n\\\\nQ: Can I put my apex (example.com) directly on Manus?\\\\n\\\\n* Potentially\\\\u2014if your DNS supports ALIAS/ANAME or Cloudflare CNAME Flattening to the Manus hostname. Otherwise, redirect apex \\\\u2192 www and point www \\\\u2192 Manus via CNAME.\\\\n\\\\nQ: How long does SSL take?\\\\n\\\\n* Typically minutes after DNS validates, based on common ACME behavior; allow some buffer and recheck DNS if delayed.\\\\n\\\\nQ: How do I roll back a bad release?\\\\n\\\\n* Manus 1.5 highlights versioning and rollbacks; revert to a prior version and your DNS can stay unchanged. The platform\\\\u2019s [1.5 release note](https://manus.im/blog/manus-1.5-release) mentions tracked changes and rollbacks.\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## Summary checklist (keep for future launches)\\\\n\\\\n* Choose canonical: example.com or www.example.com (or app.example.com)\\\\n* Subdomain \\\\u2192 CNAME \\\\u2192 Manus hostname (copy from Manus UI)\\\\n* Apex strategy: ALIAS/ANAME, CNAME Flattening, or redirect to www\\\\n* Propagation: set low TTL during cutover; verify via dig/nslookup\\\\n* SSL: ensure status turns active; test with curl -I and browser\\\\n* Redirects: one canonical path with 301; preserve paths\\\\n* Post-launch: analytics visible; mixed content resolved; version ready for rollback\\\\n\\\\nIf you want to formalize this into a reusable checklist for your team, you can also [build a repeatable launch checklist](https://skywork.ai/skypage/en/From-Chaos-to-Closeout%3A-How-I-Use-AI-Checklist-Generators-to-Master-Construction-Punch-Lists-in-2025/1975594223593517056) and adapt it for web releases.\\\\n\\\\nPost Views: 307\\\\n\\\\n### About The Author\\\\n\\\\n![](https://skywork.ai/blog/wp-content/cache/flying-press/gravatar-64fb935dd733.png)\\\\n\\\\n[#### searchResults.querySelectorAll(\'.search-result-item\').forEach(item => {\n            item.addEventListener(\'click\', () => {\n                window.location.href = item.dataset.url;\n searchResults.style.display = \'none\';\n        }\n    }\n    \n    showSearchError() {\n        console.log(\'Search error - showing error message\');\n    }\n    \n    // ===== MOBILE MENU =====\n { \'Content-Type\': \'application/json\' },\n            credentials: \'include\', // Important for cross-site cookies\n            body: JSON.stringify(credentials)\n        });\n        \n        return response.json();\n    }\n    \n    async checkSession() {\n        const response = await fetch(`${RAILWAY_CONFIG.apiUrl}/auth/session`, {\n            credentials: \'include\'\n        });\n        \n        return response.ok ? response.json() : null;\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## ğŸ”„ PHASE 5: WEBSOCKET INTEGRATION\n\n### ğŸ“‹ STEP 6: REAL-TIME DATA SYNC\n\n**6.1 WebSocket WebSocket(\'wss://helix-unified-production.up.railway.app/ws\');\n        this.reconnectAttempts = 0;\n        this.maxReconnectAttempts = 5;\n    }\n    \n    connect() {\n        this.ws.onopen = () => {\n            console.log(\'Helix WebSocket connected\');\n            this.sendAuthentication();\n        };\n        \n        this.ws.onmessage = (event) => {\n            const data = JSON.parse(event.data);\n            this.handleMessage(data);\n        };\n        \n        this.ws.onclose = () => {\n            console.log(\'WebSocket disconnected, attempting reconnect...\');\n            this.reconnect();\n        };\n    }\n    \n    sendAuthentication() {\n        this.ws.send(JSON.stringify({\n            type: \'auth\',\n            token: this.getAuthToken()\n        }));\n    }\n    \n    handleMessage(data) {\n        switch (data.type) {\n            case \'status_update\':\n                this.updateSiteStatus(data.payload);\n                break;\n            case \'ucf_update\':\n                this.updateUCFDisplay(data.payload);\n                break;\n            case \'notification\':\n                this.showNotification(data.payload);\n                break;\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**6.2 Cross-Site Event Broadcasting**\n```javascript\n// Broadcast events to all connected sites\nfunction broadcastEvent(eventType, payload) {\n    fetch(`${RAILWAY_CONFIG.apiUrl}/broadcast`, {\n        method: \'POST\',\n        headers: { \'Content-Type\': \'application/json\' },\n        body: JSON.stringify({\n            type: eventType,\n            payload: payload,\n            timestamp: Date.now()\n        })\n    });\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## ğŸ“Š PHASE 6: MONITORING SETUP\n\n### ğŸ“‹ STEP 7: PERFORMANCE MONITORING\n\n**7.1 Google
